Qin and Mudabbir: One Rule, Different Payment
Ruling statement with comparative expansion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on recourse for a qin slave and identify the sole difference from a mudabbir.

Core Idea
Qin equals mudabbir in all recourse rules; only the payment differs: slave itself vs. value.

This short passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq establishes a critical principle in Hanafi diyat: the fully-owned slave (qin) is treated identically to the mudabbir (slave promised freedom after the master's death) when it comes to the master's right of recourse against a usurper after compensating a victim. The only difference is practical—the master hands over the slave itself for a qin, but pays its monetary value for a mudabbir. The same intra-Hanafi disagreement applies, making this a concise anchor for a recurring theme.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and the comparison
The subject is the treatment of a qin (fully-owned slave) in the specific situation of recourse after paying compensation for a crime committed by the slave. The text compares it directly to the mudabbir, stating they are alike.
Qin is the default slave category; mudabbir is a slave with a promise of freedom after the master's death.
2
Note the sole exception
The only difference between qin and mudabbir is what the master pays to the victim's heir: for a qin, the master hands over the slave itself; for a mudabbir, he pays the slave's monetary value. All other rules—especially the right of recourse against the usurper—are identical.
The term 'يدلع' (yadla‘) in the source is a variant spelling of 'يدفع' (yadfa‘), meaning 'pays'.
3
Understand the scenario triggering recourse
The text provides a scenario: a man usurps (gains control by force) a slave. The slave then commits a crime while in the usurper's possession. The slave is returned to the master, and then commits another crime. The master must pay compensation for the second crime. He then seeks recourse from the usurper for the loss incurred.
This mirrors the exact scenario discussed for the mudabbir in the previous lesson.
4
Recognize the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The same disagreement among Hanafi imams applies: Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani's view as transmitted by some) allow the master to seek recourse from the usurper after paying. Muhammad al-Shaybani (in another view) does not allow recourse if it would result in the master owning both the slave and a substitute (the usurper's payment) simultaneously.
This ikhtilaf arises from the principle that one cannot combine the original and its substitute in ownership.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( والقن كالمدبر غير أن المولى يدلع العبد هنا وثمة القيمة) أي العبد القن فيما ذكرنا كالمدبر، ولا فرق بينهما إلا أن المولى يدفع القن وفي المدبر القيمة حتى إذا غصب رجل عبداً فجنى في يده ثم رده على المولى فجنى عنده جناية أخرى فإن المولى يدفعه إلى الأول ثم يرجع على الغاصب عندهما، وعند محمد لا يدفع ما أخذه من الغاصب إلى الأول بل يسلم له فلا يتصور الرجوع على الغاصب ثانياً على ما ذكرنا في المدبر
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And the qin [full slave] is like the mudabbir, except that the master pays the slave here and there the value), meaning the fully-owned slave in what we mentioned is like the mudabbir, and there is no difference between them except that the master pays the slave [qin] and in the mudabbir [pays] the value. So if a man usurped a slave and he [the slave] committed a crime in his hand, then he returned him to the master, and he [the slave] committed another crime in his presence, then the master pays him [the slave] to the first [victim's heir] and then seeks recourse from the usurper according to them [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad]. According to Muhammad, he does not pay what he took from the usurper to the first, but it becomes settled in his favor, so recourse from the usurper a second time is inconceivable, as we mentioned in the mudabbir.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This is a brief ruling from al-Bahr al-Raiq equating the treatment of a fully-owned slave (qin) with that of a mudabbir in the context of recourse against a usurper. The only difference is practical: for a qin, the master hands over the slave itself as compensation to the first victim; for a mudabbir, he pays its monetary value. The underlying legal logic is identical. The same intra-Hanafi disagreement applies: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow recourse after payment, while Muhammad (al-Shaybani) prevents it if it would lead to combining the slave and its substitute in the master's ownership. The passage serves as a concise memorization anchor for this equivalence.

Key Terms
القن (al-qinn): A fully-owned slave without any restriction like tadbir.
يدلع (yadla‘): Passes, pays, or hands over (in this context, the master hands over the slave to the victim's heir).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the only difference between a qin and a mudabbir in the recourse scenario?
A) The master may not seek recourse for a qin, only for a mudabbir
B) The master pays the slave itself for a qin and its value for a mudabbir
C) The master pays the value for a qin and the slave itself for a mudabbir
D) There is no difference at all

Key Takeaway
A qin is treated identically to a mudabbir in all aspects of recourse after compensating for a slave's crime, with the sole exception that the master pays the slave itself for a qin and its monetary value for a mudabbir.

Usurped Slaves and Multiple Homicides: The Hanafi Dispute on Recourse
Presents a complex case from al-Mabsut involving two usurped slaves and multiple homicides

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the master's right of recourse for damages to usurped slaves and explain the basis for the disagreement.

Core Idea
When a usurped slave causes loss, Abu Hanifa grants full recourse to the master; the Sahibayn limit it.

This passage from al-Mabsut presents a complex scenario: two usurped slaves commit homicides, then one kills the other. The key question is whether the master can recover the value of the slain female slave from the usurper. This intra-Hanafi disagreement reveals fundamental principles about liability during usurpation.

Guided Path
1
Identify parties and events
Determine the sequence: a man usurps a male slave and a female slave; each kills a man by mistake; then the male slave kills the female slave; the male slave is returned to the master.
2
State the master's liabilities
Identify what the master must pay: the value of the female slave to her victim's heir, and the value of the male slave to his victim's heir (or the male slave itself).
3
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa allows the master to recover the value of the female slave from the usurper because the cause for that value arose while the slaves were in the usurper's possession. Also, if the master pays the male slave, he recovers its full value from the usurper.
4
State the Sahibayn's position
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, the master cannot recover the value of the female slave. For the male slave, the master pays it partly to the victim's heir and partly to the usurper (e.g., 11 shares). The master then seeks recourse for the male slave's value from the usurper.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المبسوط : وإذا غصب رجل عبداً وجارية فقتل كل واحد رجلاً خطأ ثم قتل العبد الجارية ورد العبد فإنه يرد معه قيمة الجارية فيدفعها المولى إلى ولي قتيل الجارية ويرجع بها على الغاصب لأن قيمة الجارية استحقت من يد المولى بسبب كان عند الغاصب عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله. وعندهما لا يرجع وإن اختار الدفع دفع العبد كله إلى ولي قتيل العبد فدفع في قياس قول أبي حنيفة ويرجع بقيمته على الغاصب، وعندهما يدفعه إلى ولي قتيل العبد وإلى الغاصب على أحد عشر سهماً إذا كانت قيمة الجارية ألف درهم سنهم للغاصب وعشرة لولي قتيل العبد، ثم يرجع المولى على الغاصب بقيمة العبد فيدفع منها إلى ولي قتيله جزءاً من
And in al-Mabsut: If a man usurped a male slave and a female slave, and each killed a man by mistake, then the male slave killed the female slave and returned the male slave, then he returns with him the value of the female slave, so the master pays it to the guardian of the female slave's victim and seeks recourse from the usurper for it, because the value of the female slave became due from the master's hand by a cause that was with the usurper according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. And according to them [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], he does not seek recourse. And if he chooses to pay, he pays the entire male slave to the guardian of the male slave's victim; so he pays in accordance with the analogy of Abu Hanifa's statement and seeks recourse for his value from the usurper. And according to them, he pays it to the guardian of the male slave's victim and to the usurper in eleven shares: if the value of the female slave is one thousand dirhams, a share for the usurper and ten for the guardian of the male slave's victim. Then the master seeks recourse from the usurper for the value of the male slave and pays from it to the guardian of his victim a portion...
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage from al-Mabsut (a core book of zahir al-riwaya) presents a relevant case: a man usurps two slaves (a male and a female). Each slave commits an accidental homicide. Then the male slave kills the female slave. The male slave is returned to the master. The master must pay the value of the female slave to her victim's heir. According to Abu Hanifa, he can then recover that amount from the usurper because the cause for the female's value arose from the usurper's possession. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad disagree, saying he cannot recover. There is also an alternative payment method: the master can pay the entire male slave to the male slave's victim. Following Abu Hanifa's analogy, the master then recovers the male slave's value from the usurper. According to the two, the master pays the male slave partly to the victim and partly to the usurper in a ratio (11 shares example given). The passage illustrates the practical application of the principles discussed earlier and shows the same intra-Hanafi disagreement. Note: the passage seems incomplete as it cuts off mid-sentence.

Key Terms
الجارية (al-jāriyah): A female slave.
خطأ (khaṭa’): Mistake or unintentional act; here, accidental homicide.
غصب (ghaṣb): Usurpation; wrongful taking of property without owner's consent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the female slave was killed by the male slave
B) Because the cause for the value arose from the usurper's possession
C) Because the usurper is liable for all crimes
D) Because the master paid the value voluntarily

Key Takeaway
In cases of usurped slaves committing crimes, Abu Hanifa allows recourse for consequential losses; the Sahibayn limit it to direct damages only.

Master's Recovery from Usurper for Mudabbir's Double Crime
Commentary on a ruling with causation (talil)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a mudabbir usurped twice with crimes and explain the master's recovery rights from the usurper.

Core Idea
When both crimes occur in the usurper's possession, the master recovers the full value plus the half he pays to the first heir from the same usurper.

This lesson examines a specific scenario where a mudabbir (deferred manumission slave) is usurped twice, committing a crime in each usurpation. The master is liable for the slave's value due to the mudabbir's protected status, but he can recover the entire value from the final usurper. Moreover, he recovers an additional half that he must pay to the first heir. We will trace the reasoning behind this complex liability and the intra-Hanafi discussion about its consistency with similar cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
The mudabbir is first usurped, commits a crime, is returned to the master, then usurped again and commits a second crime.
Both crimes occur while the slave is in the usurper's possession (not the master's).
2
Determine the Master's Liability
The master must pay the full value of the mudabbir to the heirs of the two victims, divided equally.
Liability arises because the mudabbir is not surrendered due to tadbir, so the master compensates the victims.
3
Trace the Recourse Against the Usurper
The master recovers the full value from the second usurper because both crimes occurred in his hands.
This is unlike earlier cases where a crime occurred in the master's possession.
4
Analyze the Additional Half Recovery
The master pays half to the first heir but then recovers that half from the same usurper, as the first heir's original entitlement was reduced by the second crime.
The half is due to a cause in the usurper's possession, so the master recoups it.
5
Note the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Some scholars disagree on whether the master recovers this half, analogizing to earlier cases where recovery was limited.
The text upholds the distinction per Muhammad al-Shaybani, and the matn's ruling is relied upon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الديات باب غصب العبد والمدبر والصبي والجناية في ذلك
القيمة مدبر جنى عند غاصبه فرده فغصبه أخرى فجنى فعلى سيده قيمته لهما ورجع بقيمته على الغاصب ودفع نصفها إلى الأول ورجع بذلك النصف على الغاصب
غصب عند المولى أولاً ثم غصبه فجنى في يده ثم رده إلى المولى دفعه إلى ولي الجنايتين نصفين ثم يرجع بنصف قيمته على الغاصب لما ذكرنا . قال رحمه الله : مدبر جنى عند غاصبه فرده فغصبه أخرى فجنى فعلى سيده قيمته لهما أي إذا غصب رجل مدبراً فجنى عنده جناية فرده على المولى ثم غصبه ثانياً فجنى عنده جناية أخرى فعلى المولى قيمته بين ولي الجنايتين نصفين لأن منعه بالتدبير فوجب عليه قيمته على ما بينا . قال رحمه الله : ( ورجع بقيمته على الغاصب) لأن الجنايتين كانت في يد الغاصب فاستحق كل بسبب كان في يده فرجع عليه بالكل بخلاف المسائل المتقدمة فإن هناك استحق النصف كان عنده والنصف بسبب كان في يد المالك فيرجع : بالنصف لذلك. قال رحمه الله : ودفع نصفها إلى (الأول) أي دفع المولى نصف القيمة المأخوذة من الغاصب ثانياً إلى ولي الجناية الأولى لأنه استحق كل القيمة لعدم المزاحمة عند وجود جنايته وإنما انتقص حقه بحكم المزاحمة من بعد . قال رحمه الله : ( ورجع بذلك النصف على الغاصب أي يرجع المولى بالنصف الذي دفعه ثانياً إلى ولي الجناية الأولى على الغاصب لأن ولي الجناية الأولى استحق هذا النصف كان في يد الغاصب فيرجع عليه به ويسلم الباقي له ولا يدفعه إلى ولي الجناية الأولى لأنه استوفى حقه في حقه ولا إلى ولي الثانية لأنه لا حق له إلا في النصف لسبق حق الأول عليه وقد وصل ذلك إليه، وهذا لأن الثاني يستحق النصف لوجود المزاحمة وقت جنايته والمزاحمة موجودة فبقي على ما كان بخلاف ولي الأولى لأنه استحق الكل وقت الجناية، وإنما حقه إلى النصف للمزاحمة قالوا وكلما وجد شيئاً من بدل العبد أخذه رجع حتى يستوفي حقه، ثم قيل هذه المسألة على الخلاف كالأولى، وقيل على الاتفاق، والفرق لمحمد أن الذي يرجع به ولي الجناية الأولى عوض ما سلم له في المسألة الأولى لأن الثانية كانت في يد المالك فلو دفع إليه ثانياً تكرر الاستحقاق، وأما في هذه المسألة فيمكن أن يجعله عوضاً عن الجناية الثانية لأنها كانت في يد الغاصب فلا يؤدي إلى ما ذكرنا.
Book of Retaliation, Chapter on Usurpation of the Slave, Mudabbir, and Child, and Offenses Therein. The value: a mudabbir committed a crime with his usurper, then he returned him, then he usurped him again, and he committed a crime, so upon his master is its value for the two (heirs), and he recovers its value from the usurper, and he pays half of it to the first (heir), and he recovers that half from the usurper. He said: a mudabbir committed a crime with his usurper, so he returned him, then he usurped him again and he committed a crime, so upon his master is its value for the two, meaning: if a man usurped a mudabbir, and he committed a crime with him, and he returned him to the master, then he usurped him a second time, and he committed another crime with him, then upon the master is its value between the heirs of the two crimes in halves. He said: and he recovers its value from the usurper, because the two crimes were in the hands of the usurper, so each became due due to a cause that was in his hands, so he recovers the whole from him. He said: and he pays half of it to the first, i.e., the master pays half of the value taken from the usurper a second time to the heir of the first crime. He said: and he recovers that half from the usurper, i.e., the master recovers the half that he paid a second time to the heir of the first crime from the usurper.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a ruling from the matn regarding a mudabbir (a slave whose manumission is deferred) who commits crimes while in the hands of two successive usurpers. The ruling states that the master must pay the full value of the mudabbir to the heirs of the two victims, dividing it equally between them. The master then recovers this full value from the second usurper. However, there is an additional detail: the master pays half of the value from the usurper to the first heir and then recovers that half from the usurper as well. The reason is that at the time of the first crime, the first heir was entitled to the entire value, but due to the second crime, his share is reduced to half. Since both crimes occurred while the mudabbir was in the usurper's possession, the usurper is liable for both compensations. The commentary clarifies that this situation differs from earlier cases where the second crime occurred in the master's possession. There is a disagreement about whether this case is analogous to earlier ones or if there is consensus; according to Muhammad, the distinction is valid because the second crime here occurred in the usurper's hands.

Key Terms
مدبر (mudabbir): A slave whose manumission is deferred until after the master's death.
غاصب (ghasib): One who takes property by usurpation (ghasb) without right.
قيمة (qimah): The monetary value of the slave, used as compensation for the crime.
ولي الجناية (wali al-jinayah): The heir of the victim who has the right to claim compensation for the crime.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the mudabbir case with two crimes in the usurper's possession, from whom does the master ultimately recover the full value and the additional half paid to the first heir?
A) The first usurper
B) The second usurper
C) The mudabbir himself
D) The first heir

Key Takeaway
When both crimes occur in the usurper's possession, the master recovers the full value plus the half he must pay to the first heir, all from the same usurper.

Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Usurped Slave Killing Free Man and Slave Woman
Intra-Hanafi dispute on liability when usurped slave kills two persons.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether injury by a usurped slave against the usurper's property is considered or disregarded, and apply the ruling to scenarios of insolvency.

Core Idea
Retroactive ownership (ملك مستند) makes the slave's injury against the usurper void, but Sahibayn consider it due to potential benefit.

In this passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq, Ibn Nujaym discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute: When a usurped slave kills a free man and a slave woman belonging to the usurper, should the slave's injury against the usurper's property be considered? Abu Hanifa says no (hadar), while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say yes. This leads to different distribution of the slave's value. Let's trace the legal reasoning and practical outcomes.

Guided Path
1
State the factual scenario
Identify the key facts: a usurped slave kills two persons—a free man and a slave woman owned by the usurper.
The slave woman is the property of the usurper.
2
Identify the core legal question
The dispute hinges on whether the injury (جناية) of the slave against the usurper's property (the slave woman) is considered or disregarded.
If disregarded, only the free man's claim remains; if considered, the slave's value is divided.
3
Present Abu Hanifa's view and proof
Abu Hanifa holds that the usurper becomes owner of the slave retroactively (ملك مستند) from the day of usurpation. Thus the slave's act appears as injury against his own master, which is null (هدر). Therefore, only the free man's claim exists, and the slave is paid entirely to his guardian.
Key concept: retroactive ownership nullifies injury against the owner.
4
Present the Sahibayn's view and proof
The Sahibayn argue that considering the injury brings a benefit (فائدة) to the usurper—for example, through ransom he may receive more than the slave's value. Hence the injury is considered, and the slave's value is divided proportionally between the free man's guardian and the usurper's claim.
They prioritize utility over retroactive logic.
5
Compare practical outcomes and special cases
Under Abu Hanifa, the free man's guardian gets the entire slave; under the Sahibayn, the slave is divided 10/11 to the free man and 1/11 to the usurper (if values are as stated). The text also discusses insolvency of the usurper and the option of the guardian to wait.
The difference matters in how compensation is calculated and distributed.

وجناية المغصوب على الغاصب وعلى ماله هدر ،عنده وعندهما معتبرة لما تبين فعنده لما هدرت جناية العبد على الجارية بقي في رقبته جناية واحدة وهو دم الحر فيدفع كله إلى ولي دم الحر ويفديه كله إليه وهو مضطر في Because all of the book of diyat, chapter on usurpation of a slave, a mudabbar, a child, and injury in that, eleven parts, then he returns with that to the usurper. This is based on the fact that when the usurper owned the slave girl by guarantee from the day of usurpation, it appears that the slave killed an owned slave girl, and the injury of the usurped [slave] against the usurper and his property is disregarded according to him, but according to them it is considered as will become clear. Then he returns its value and pays to the guardian of their slain completely because his right was established in all of the slave, and ten parts of the slave reached him, and one part did not reach him, and in the hand of the master is its substitute, so he had the right to take that from him. Then he returns upon the usurper with the like of that as we explained. And for the guardian of the slain slave girl, he may take from the master ten parts of her value in one narration because the substitute of all the slave girl reached him, because the slave stood in place of the slave girl. And if its value is less than the value of the slave girl because when a low value thing kills a high value thing and is paid with it, it stands in place of all of it. So when the slave stands in place of all the slave girl, it becomes as if all the slave girl reached him, unlike the guardian of the slain slave because his right was in all of the slave and did not transfer to its substitute, and some of the slave reached him, so he had the right to take the substitute of what did not reach him of the slave. And if the usurped slave kills the usurper, his blood is disregarded, and likewise the mortgaged slave if he kills the mortgagee according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, and according to them it is considered so that the master is ordered to pay or ransom. For them, there is benefit in considering his injury because the usurper owns him by payment with value, and he owns another's slave with value beneficially, as if he bought from him, and by ransom he owns his own blood money, which is apparently more than the value, so the usurper gains an increase over the value, indicating that there is benefit in considering this slave girl, so it is obligatory to consider it. And Allah knows best. And for Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, that when the master takes the guarantee from the usurper, the usurper owns the slave retroactively to the time of usurpation, and its apparent meaning is that the injury appeared from the owned [slave] against his owner, and the injury of the owned [slave] against his owner is disregarded because the master does not owe anything against his slave, and the injury of the usurped [slave] against his master is considered according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, contrary to them as previously in the chapter on pledge.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the case of a usurped slave (عبد مغصوب) who kills two persons: a free man and a slave woman belonging to the usurper. The key issue is whether the injury of the slave against the usurper's property is considered (معتبرة) or disregarded (هدر). Abu Hanifa holds that since the usurper becomes owner of the slave retroactively from the date of usurpation (by way of ضمان), the slave's injury against the usurper's property is disregarded, leaving only the claim of the free man's guardian. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the injury is considered, so the slave's value is divided proportionally between the two victims' guardians and the usurper's claim. The text details the different distributions, including scenarios where the usurper is insolvent. The argument hinges on the nature of ownership by guarantee and whether retroactive ownership affects the validity of the slave's actions. The proof for Abu Hanifa is that once the master takes compensation, the usurper's ownership relates back, making the slave's act against his own master (the usurper) void. The Sahibayn argue that considering the injury produces a benefit for the usurper (e.g., he may get a higher value through ransom), so it should be considered. The passage ends by noting that according to Abu Hanifa, the same principle applies if the usurped slave kills the usurper himself: it is disregarded. The dispute is based on usul principles regarding the effect of ضمان and the nature of injury by a slave.

Key Terms
هدر (hadar): Disregarded, null, having no legal effect.
ملك مستند (mulk mustanid): Ownership that relates back retroactively to a prior time.
ضمان (daman): Guarantee or liability to pay compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is the injury of a usurped slave against the usurper's property disregarded?
A) Because the slave is not fully owned by the usurper
B) Because the usurper's ownership relates back, making the slave's act against his own owner
C) Because the usurper has not yet paid the value
D) Because the slave is free from liability

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, when a usurper becomes owner retroactively, injury by the usurped slave against the usurper's property is disregarded, affecting the distribution of compensation.

Diyat — Blood Money

Ruling on Usurping a Free Child Who Dies
Ruling with proof on liability when free child dies in usurper's hands.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability when a free child dies in the usurper's hands and distinguish between death from common causes and death from transgressive acts such as moving to dangerous places.

Core Idea
Usurping a free child creates liability for destruction, not usurpation, if death is caused by transgressive causation.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains a key Hanafi distinction: the usurper of a free child is not liable if the child dies suddenly or from fever, but is liable if death results from moving the child to a place of danger. This ruling is based on istihsan, overriding the qiyas that would deny any liability since a free person cannot be usurped. Understanding this principle clarifies when indirect acts (tasabbub) create liability for blood money (diyah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its two scenarios
Determine what act is being discussed (usurping a free child) and the two types of death: (1) sudden/fever, (2) lightning/snakebite. Note the different rulings.
The act is 'غصب صبياً حراً'. The first scenario has no liability; the second has diyah on the 'aqila.
2
Distinguish qiyas from istihsan
Recognize that qiyas would deny liability in both cases because usurpation of a free person is not recognized. However, istihsan imposes liability in the second case based on the principle of transgressive causation (tasabbub).
The text explicitly states: 'وهذا استحسان والقياس أن لا يضمن'.
3
Trace the reasoning for istihsan
Understand the logical steps: The usurper's act of moving the child to a dangerous place is a form of destruction (إتلاف) via causation. Since the child cannot be owned, the liability is based on destruction, not usurpation. The transgression lies in removing the child from the safe custody of the guardian.
The text compares to digging a hole in the road: condition of the cause is like the cause when transgression occurs.
4
Apply the distinction to the child as depositor
Examine the secondary case: a child deposits a slave and kills it versus deposits food and eats it. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that the child's 'aqila is liable for killing the slave but not for eating food. Abu Yusuf holds liability in both.
The difference is linked to the nature of the act: killing is destruction, eating is consumption without destruction of a deposit.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf and its implications
Understand that Abu Yusuf disagrees with Abu Hanifa and Muhammad on the depository child cases. This affects rulings on other transactions like acknowledgment and borrowing.
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, as the text presents their view first.

قال رحمه الله : (غصب صبياً حراً فمات في يده فجأة أو بحمى لم يضمن وإن مات بصاعقة أو نهش حية فديته على عاقلة الغاصب وهذا استحسان والقياس أن لا يضمن في الوجهين وهو قول زفر والشافعي رحمهما الله تعالى لأن الغصب في الحر لا يتحقق ألا ترى أنه لا يتحقق في المكاتب وإن كان صغيراً لكونه حراً يداً مع أنه رقيق رقبة فالحر يداً، ورقبة أولى أن لا يضمن به وجه الاستحسان أن هذا ضمان إتلاف لا ضمان غصب والصبي يضمن بالاتلاف، وهذا لأن نقله إلى أرض مسبعة أو إلى مكان الصواعق إتلاف منه تسبباً وهو متعد فيه بتفويت يد الحافظ وهو المولى فيضمن وهذا لأن الحيات والسباع والصواعق لا تكون في كل مكان فأمكن حفظه عنده فإذا نقله إليه وهو متعد فيه فقد أزال حفظ المولى عنده معتدياً فيضاف إليه لأن شرط العلة بمنزلة العلة إذا كان تعدياً كالحفر في الطريق بخلاف الموت فجأة أو بحمى فإن ذلك لا يختلف باختلاف الأماكن حتى لو نقله إلى مكان تغلب فيه الحمى والأمراض يقول إنه يضمن وتجب الدية على العاقلة لكونه قتلاً تسبباً بخلاف المكاتب لأنه في يد نفسه، وإن كان صغيراً فهو يلحق بالكثير ألا : تری أنه لا يزوج إلا برضاه كالبالغ والحر الصغير يزوجه وليه بدون رضاه فإذا أخرجه من يد المولى فمات مما يمكن التحرز عنه يضمن والمكاتب لا يعجز عن حفظ نفسه فلا يضمن بالغصب كالحر الكبير لو لم يمكنه من حفظ نفسه فلا يضمن بالغصب مما صنع من قيد ونحوه يضمن المكاتب، وكالحر الكبير أيضاً كما يضمن الصغير لأنه حينئذ يكون التلف مضافاً إلى الغاصب بتقصير حفظه . قال رحمه الله : كصبي أودع عبداً فقتله وإن أودع طعاماً وأكله لم يضمن أي يضمن عاقلة الغاصب كما يضمن عاقلة الصبي إذا قتل عبداً أودع. عنده، وهذا الفرق بين العبد المودع والطعام المودع هو قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد وقال أبو يوسف والشافعي رحمهما الله تعالى : تضمن الصبي المودع في الوجهين وعلى هذا لو أودع العبد المحجور عليه مالاً فاستهلكه لا يؤخذ بالضمان في الحال عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى ويؤخذ به بعد العتق وعند أبي يوسف والشافعي رحمهما الله تعالى يؤخذ به في الحال، وعلى هذا الخلاف الإقرار في العبد والوصي وكذا الإعارة فيهما . ثم أن محمداً رحمه الله شرط في الجامع أن يكون الصبي عاقلاً. وفي الجامع
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: '(If he usurps a free child and he dies in his hand suddenly or from fever, he does not guarantee; but if he dies from a lightning bolt or a snakebite, his blood money is upon the 'aqila of the usurper. This is istihsan, and by qiyas he would not guarantee in both cases, and it is the saying of Zufar and al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on them, because usurpation of a free person is not actualized; do you not see that it is not actualized in the mukatab even if he is young because he is free in hand while he is a slave in neck? So a free person in hand and neck is more deserving that one does not guarantee by him. The aspect of istihsan is that this is a guarantee of destruction, not a guarantee of usurpation, and the child is guaranteed by destruction. This is because transporting him to a land of wild beasts or to a place of lightning is destruction by him as causation, and he is transgressing in it by removing the hand of the protector, which is the master, so he guarantees. And this is because snakes, wild beasts, and lightning are not in every place, so it was possible to protect him with him, but when he transported him while being transgressing, he has removed the protection of the master with transgression, so it is attributed to him because the condition of the cause is like the cause when there is transgression, like digging in the road. Unlike death suddenly or from fever, for that does not differ with difference of places. So if he transported him to a place where fevers and diseases prevail, he says that he does guarantee and the blood money is obligatory upon the 'aqila because it is a killing by causation. Unlike the mukatab because he is in his own hand, even if he is young, he is joined to the mature. Do you not see that he is not married except with his consent like the adult, while the free child is married by his guardian without his consent? So if he takes him out from the hand of the master and he dies from something that can be guarded against, he guarantees. And the mukatab is not incapable of guarding himself, so he does not guarantee by usurpation, like the free adult. If he cannot guard himself, then he does not guarantee by usurpation; but if he does something like tying him, then he guarantees the mukatab, and like the free adult also as he guarantees the child because then the destruction is attributed to the usurper due to negligence in guarding. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'Like a child who deposits a slave and kills him, and if he deposits food and eats it, he does not guarantee.' That is, the 'aqila of the usurper guarantees, just as the 'aqila of the child guarantees if he kills a deposited slave according to him. And this difference between the deposited slave and the deposited food is the saying of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on them, said: The depository child guarantees in both cases. And upon this, if the interdicted child deposits wealth and consumes it, he is not taken with the guarantee immediately according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, and he is taken with it after emancipation. According to Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on them, he is taken with it immediately. And upon this is the difference in acknowledgment by the slave and the executor, and similarly borrowing in them. Then Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, stipulated in Al-Jami' that the child be sane. And in Al-Jami'...
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on usurping a free child (صبياً حراً) and the liability if the child dies. The text distinguishes between two scenarios: (1) if the child dies suddenly or from fever, the usurper is not liable; (2) if the child dies from lightning or snakebite, the blood money (دية) is upon the 'aqila (tribal guarantors) of the usurper. This is an example of istihsan (juristic preference), because by qiyas (analogy) one would not be liable in either case, as usurpation of a free person is not recognized (since a free person cannot be owned). The proof of istihsan is that this is a guarantee of destruction (ضمان إتلاف), not of usurpation. The usurper, by moving the child to a dangerous place, has caused the destruction through his transgression. The text then compares to the case of a child who deposits a slave and kills it: the child's 'aqila is liable, but if he deposits food and eats it, he is not liable (according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). This leads to an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf holds that the child is liable in both cases. The same principle applies to other transactions like borrowing. Finally, Muhammad stipulates that the child must be sane (عاقلاً) for these rulings to apply.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference, a method of reasoning where a ruling is chosen because it is more suitable or just than the analogical (qiyas) ruling.
العاقلة (al-'aqila): The group of male agnatic relatives (or tribe) who are responsible for paying blood money (diyah) on behalf of a killer who killed accidentally or unintentionally.
تسبب (tasabbub): Causation; an act that indirectly leads to death or injury.
غصب (ghasb): Usurpation; physically taking possession of someone else's property without consent and with transgression.
ضمان إتلاف (damān itlāf): Guarantee for destruction; liability for destroying property or causing loss.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school impose liability on the usurper of a free child who dies from a snakebite, even though usurpation of a free person is not recognized?
A) Because the usurper becomes the owner of the child's body
B) Because it is a case of guarantee of destruction (ضمان إتلاف) through transgressive causation
C) Because the child's family can sue for loss of service
D) Because the 'aqila of the usurper is responsible for all deaths on their property

Key Takeaway
Usurpation of a free child does not create a guarantee of usurpation, but transgressive causation of death imposes diyah on the usurper's 'aqila as a guarantee of destruction (damān itlāf).

Definition and Conditions of Qasamah
Defines qasamah and lists its conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the legal definition of qasamah and list its essential conditions according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Qasamah is a procedural oath by fifty men from a locality to establish blood-money liability when a killer is unknown.

This lesson introduces qasamah, a unique Islamic legal institution for unresolved homicides. You will learn its precise definition, its pillar, and the detailed conditions that must be met for qasamah to be valid. The Hanafi school's systematic approach to these conditions provides a clear framework for this serious matter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal definition
Read the opening lines of the passage to extract the definition of qasamah: a sworn oath by fifty men from the locality where the body is found, sworn by the chosen representatives on behalf of the community.
The definition is implied in the matn: 'fifty men from them... swear By Allah we did not kill him.'
2
Distinguish pillar from conditions
Note the author's distinction between the rukn (pillar) – the utterance of the oath – and the shurut (conditions) – the requirements that must be present for the oath to be valid.
The rukn is the act of swearing; conditions are external to the oath itself.
3
List the conditions
Go through each condition stated in the passage: swearers are free adult males, victim has trace of killing, killer unknown, victim human, claim by guardians, denial by defendants, demand by guardians, place owned or possessed.
Memorize these conditions; they are the core of the ruling.
4
Note the proof and cause
Identify that the proof (dalil) is the well-known hadiths and consensus, and the cause (sabab) is the finding of the body in the locality.
The cause triggers the obligation of qasamah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الديات باب القسامة
قتيل وجد في محلة لم يدر قاتله حلف خمسون رجلاً منهم يتخيرهم الولي بالله ما قتلناه
يقسم خمسون رجلاً من أهل المحلة كل منهم يقول بالله ما قتلته ولا علمت له قاتلاً ا هـ . أقول : ما ذكر في النهاية إنما هو مسألة القسامة شرعاً فإن التفسير من قبيل التصورات وما ذكر فيها تصديق من قبيل الشرطيات كما ترى، نعم يمكن أن يؤخذ منه تفسير القسامة شرعاً بتدقيق النظر لكنه في موضع بيان معنى القسامة شرعاً في أول الباب تعسف خارج عن سنن الطريق. وأما ركنها فهو أنه يجري من أن يقسم هذه الكلمات التي يقسم بها على لسانه ثم قال في النهاية : وأما شرطها فهو أن يكون المقسم رجلاً بالغاً عاقلاً حراً فلذلك لم يدخل في القسامة المرأة والصبي والمجنون والعبد وأن يكون في الميت الموجود أثر القتل، وأما لو وجد ميتاً لا أثر به فلا قسامة ولا دية، ومن شرطها أيضاً تكميل اليمين بالخمسين ا هـ . وفي غاية البيان أيضاً كذلك. ومن شروطها أيضاً أن لا يعلم قاتله فإن علم فلا قسامة فيه ولكن يجب القصاص فيه أو الدية كما تقدم. ومنها أن يكون القتيل من بني آدم فلا قسامة في بهيمة وجدت في محلة قوم، ومنها الدعوى من أولياء القتيل لأن القسامة يمين واليمين لا تجب بدون الدعوى كما في سائر الدعاوى، ومنها إنكار المدعى عليه لأن اليمين وظيفة المنكر، ومنها المطالبة في القسامة لأن اليمين حق المدعي وحق الإنسان يوفي عند طلبه كما في سائر الأموال، ومنها أن يكون الموضع الذي وجد فيه القتيل ملكاً لأحد أو في يد أحد فإن لم يكن ملكاً لأحد ولا في يد أحد أصلاً فلا قسامه فيه ولا دية في قن أو مدبر أو أم ولد أو مكاتب أو مأذون وجد مقتولاً في دار مولاه؛ نص في البدائع على هاتيك الشروط كلها بالوجه الذي ذكرناه مع زيادة تفصيل وأورد على اشتراط الحرية إذا وجد قتيل في دار مكاتب فعليه القسامة. إذا حلف يجب الأقل من قيمته ومن الدية؛ نص عليه في البدائع وأجيب بأن المكاتب حريداً، وإن لم يكن حراً رقبة كما صرحوا به في الباب السابق فوجد فيه الحرية في الجملة فجاز اشتراطنا الحرية في بناء على ذلك لكن لا يخفى ما فيه. وأما صفتها فهي وجوب الأيمان. وأما دليلها فالأحاديث المشهور وإجماع الأمة. وأما سببها فوجود القتيل في المحلة وما في معناه .
Book of Blood-Money, Chapter of Qasamah. A slain person found in a locality whose killer is unknown: fifty men from them, chosen by the guardian, swear 'By Allah, we did not kill him and we do not know his killer'. Fifty men from the people of the locality each say 'By Allah, I did not kill him and I do not know his killer'. End quote. I say: What is mentioned in al-Nihayah is the matter of qasamah legally; verily the interpretation is from the category of concepts, and what is mentioned therein is affirmation from the category of hypotheticals as you see. Yes, a legal interpretation of qasamah can be derived from it with careful consideration, but to place it in the context of explaining the meaning of qasamah legally at the beginning of the chapter is far-fetched and outside the norm. As for its pillar, it is that the swearer proceeds to swear these words which he swears with his tongue. Then he said in al-Nihayah: As for its condition, it is that the swearer be a man, adult, sane, free; hence the woman, boy, insane person, and slave are not included in qasamah. And that there be in the dead body a trace of killing. As for if a dead body is found with no trace, then no qasamah and no blood-money. And among its conditions is also completion of the oath by fifty. End quote. And in Ghayat al-Bayan likewise. And among its conditions is also that his killer be unknown; if known, no qasamah but qisas or blood-money as preceded. And among them is that the slain be from the children of Adam; no qasamah for an animal found in a people's locality. And among them is a claim from the guardians of the slain, because qasamah is an oath and an oath is not obligatory without a claim as in other claims. And among them is denial by the defendant, because the oath is the function of the denier. And among them is demand in qasamah, because the oath is the right of the claimant and a person's right is fulfilled upon his demand as in other properties. And among them is that the place where the slain is found be owned by someone or in someone's possession; if it is not owned by anyone and not in anyone's possession at all, then no qasamah and no blood-money. For a slave, mudabbar, umm walad, mukatib, or ma'dhun found slain in the house of his master, it is stated in al-Bada'i regarding all these conditions in the manner we mentioned with additional detail. And an objection was raised regarding the condition of freedom: if a slain is found in the house of a mukatib, qasamah is required. If he swears, the lesser of his value or the blood-money is obligatory; stated in al-Bada'i. And it was answered that the mukatib is free, even if not free in status as they stated in the previous chapter, so freedom in a general sense is found in him, so our condition of freedom is based on that, but it is not hidden what is in it. As for its description, it is the obligation of oaths. As for its proof, it is the well-known hadiths and consensus of the Ummah. As for its cause, it is the existence of the slain in the locality and what is in its meaning.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq defines the Islamic legal institution of qasamah. The author, commenting on the matn, first clarifies that the matn's statement is a legal ruling, not a definition. He then lists the pillars and conditions of qasamah. The pillar (rukn) is the actual utterance of the oath by the swearer. The conditions include: the swearer must be a free adult male; the victim must show signs of foul play; the killer must be unknown; the victim must be human; a claim must be filed by the guardians; the defendants must deny; the guardians must demand the oath; and the place of finding must be owned or possessed. The author also discusses a special case of a mukatib slave found slain in his master's house: qasamah applies, and the amount is the lesser of his value or the full diyah. The proof for qasamah is the well-known hadiths and ijma. The cause is the finding of the body in a locality without known killer.

Key Terms
القسامة (al-qasāmah): A sworn oath by fifty men from a locality when a body is found with unknown killer, used to establish liability for blood-money.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a condition for qasamah according to the Hanafi school?
A) The swearer may be a woman
B) The victim must be a human with trace of killing
C) The killer must be known
D) The place of finding must be unowned

Key Takeaway
Qasamah is a wajib procedure under specific conditions to resolve unknown homicides, with the oath sworn by fifty free adult males from the locality.

Diyat — Blood Money

10 min
The Qasamah Oath: Hanafi Position vs Shafi'i and Malik
Inter-madhhab dispute on qasamah procedure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on qasamah, explain the concept of lawth, and evaluate the Shafi'i/Maliki counter-argument using the hadith of the oath on the denier.

Core Idea
The oath in qasamah is on the defendants, not the guardians — the denier swears, not the claimant.

When a body is found and the killer is unknown, who must swear to exonerate? The Hanafi school holds that fifty men from the locality swear and pay blood-money, while Shafi'i and Malik require lawth (strong suspicion) to shift the oath to the guardians. This lesson unpacks the proofs and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the core Hanafi ruling: when a body is found in a locality, fifty men from that locality swear they did not kill the victim. They pay blood-money. The guardian does not swear.
This is based on the matn statement: "وإن حلفوا فعلى أهل المحلة الدية ولا يحلف الولي"
2
Define lawth as used by Shafi'i and Malik
Understand that lawth refers to strong suspicion: open enmity, a witness (even unjust), or any clear sign pointing to a specific killer.
Lawth is a condition for shifting the oath to the guardians in Shafi'i/Maliki law.
3
Present the opposing position
According to Shafi'i and Malik: if lawth exists, the guardians swear fifty oaths and receive blood-money (or qisas in Malik's view for intentional killing). If no lawth, the defendants are sworn; if they refuse, the guardians swear and get their claim.
This is explicitly stated in the source: "إذا كان هناك لوث استحلف الأولياء خمسين يميناً"
4
Examine the Hanafi proof
Analyze the hadith: 'البينة على المدعي واليمين على من أنكر' applied to blood claims. The Hanafi argument: the defendants are the deniers, so the oath is on them. There is no exception for blood.
The hadith is quoted: 'لو أعطى الناس بدعواهم لادعى رجال أموال قوم ودماءهم ولكن البينة على المدعي واليمين على من أنكر'
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical difference: Hanafi: the locality pays blood-money after the defendants swear. Shafi'i: if lawth, guardians swear and get blood-money; if no lawth, defendants swear and if they refuse, guardians swear. Malik: if lawth and claim of intentional killing, qisas may be imposed.
The dispute changes who pays, who swears, and whether retaliation is possible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال الشافعي رحمه الله : إذا كان هناك لوث استحلف الأولياء خمسين يميناً ويقضى لهم بالدية على المدعى عليه عمداً كانت الدعوى أو خطأ. وقال مالك رحمه الله : يقضى بالقود إذا كانت الدعوى في القتل أحد قولي الشافعي واللوث عندهما أن يكون هناك علامة القتل على وحد بعينه يعني العمد وهو أو ظاهر يشهد للمدعي من عداوة ظاهرة أو يشهد عدل أو جماعة غير عدول أن أهل المحلة قتلوه، وإن لم يكن ثم لوث استحلف المدعى عليهم فإن حلفوا لا دية عليهم، وإن أبوا أن يحلفوا حلف المدعي واستحق ما ادعاه لنا قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم «لو أعطى الناس بدعواهم» الحديث . وقوله البينة على المدعي واليمين على من أنكر (۱) ولا فرق في ذلك بين الدم والأموال على ظاهر الأحاديث، وما روي في قتيل وجد بين قوم قال يستحلف خمسين رجلاً منهم فهو كقول المؤلف قتيل خرج مخرج الغالب قال في العناية جرح رجل في قبيلة ولم يعلم جارحه فإما أن يصير صاحب فراش أو يكون صحيحاً بحيث يذهب ويجيء، فإن كان الثاني فلا ضمان بالاتفاق، وإن كان الأول ففيه القسامة والدية على القبيلة عند الإمام، وعند الثاني لا شيء فيه اهـ وأطلق في القتيل فشمل الخطأ والعمد والدعوى بذلك قال في الأصل : وإذا وجد قتيل في محلة قوم وادعى ولي القتيل القتل عمداً أو خطأ فهذا على ثلاثة أوجه : إما أن يدعي ولي القتيل على واحد من أهل المحلة أنه هو الذي قتله ،وليه فإن ادعى على جميع أهل المحلة أنهم قتلوا وليه عمداً أو خطأ وادعى على واحد من غير أهل المحلة أنه وليه عمداً أو خطأ وأنكر أهل المحلة فإنه يحلف خمسون رجلاً منهم كل واحد بالله ما قتلته ولا علمت له قاتلاً، فإن حلفوا غرموا الدية وإن نكلوا فإن يحبسهم حتى يحلفهم. وفي الذخيرة : هذا الحبس بدعوى العمد وإن كان يدعي الخطأ فإذا نكلوا عن اليمين يقضى عليهم بالدية اهـ. وقوله يتخيرهم «الولي يعني يختار الصالحين دون الطالحين ولو من أهل الذمة، وإن كان القتيل مدبراً أو مكاتباً وجبت القسامة وقيمته في ثلاثة سنين لأن العبد بمنزلة الأحرار في حق الدماء، وروي عن أبي يوسف أنه لا شيء فيه لأنه في حكم الأموال عنده ولا قسامة في الجنين لأنه ناقص الخلقة اهـ . قال رحمه الله : ( وإن حلفوا فعلى أهل المحلة الدية ولا يحلف الولي) وقال الشافعي رحمه الله : يحلف وقد تقدم ودليلنا قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : يحلف خمسون رجلاً منكم بالله ما قلناه ولا علمنا له قاتلاً ثم أغرموا الدية فقال الحالف : يا رسول الله يحلف ويغرم؟ فقال : نعم الحديث. هذا إذا ادعى عليهم لا بأعيانهم القتل عمداً أو خطأ لأن المدعى عليهم لا يميزون عن الباقين، ولو ادعى على البعض بأعيانهم القتل عمداً أو خطأ فكذلك الجواب وإطلاق الكتاب يدل على ذلك.
And Imam al-Shafi'i said: If there is lawth, the guardians swear fifty oaths and judgment is given for them of blood-money against the defendant, whether the claim is intentional or mistaken. And Imam Malik said: Judgment is given for retaliation if the claim is of intentional killing – one of the two opinions of al-Shafi'i. Lawth according to them is that there be a sign of killing on a specific individual, i.e., intentional killing, or an apparent circumstance that testifies for the claimant such as open enmity, or a just witness or a group of unjust witnesses that the people of the locality killed him. And if there is no lawth, the defendants are sworn; if they swear, no blood-money is on them; if they refuse to swear, the claimant swears and obtains what he claims. Our proof is the saying of the Prophet: 'If people were given according to their claims...' hadith, and his saying: 'The burden of proof is on the claimant and the oath on the denier.' There is no difference in that between blood and property based on the apparent meaning of the hadiths. And what is narrated about one killed found among a people: He said fifty men of them are sworn. It is like the author's statement: 'a slain person' appears in a general context. He said in al-Inayah: A man is wounded in a tribe and his injurer is unknown; either he becomes bedridden or is healthy so that he goes about. If the second, no liability by agreement. If the first, there is qasamah and blood-money on the tribe according to Imam Abu Hanifa; according to the second [Abu Yusuf?] there is nothing. And he spoke generally about the slain, so it includes mistaken and intentional and claim accordingly. He said in al-Asl: If a slain is found in a people's locality and the guardian of the slain claims intentional or mistaken killing, this is of three cases: either the guardian claims against one specific person of the locality that he killed him; or he claims against all the people of the locality that they killed his relative intentionally or mistakenly; or he claims against one person not from the locality. And the people of the locality deny. Then fifty men of them swear each: 'By Allah, I did not kill him and I do not know his killer.' If they swear, they pay the blood-money; if they refuse, they are imprisoned until they swear. In al-Dhakhirah: This imprisonment is for the claim of intentional killing; if the claim is mistaken, when they refuse the oath, judgment is given against them for blood-money. And his saying: 'the guardian chooses them' means he chooses the righteous, not the wicked, even from the People of the Book. And if the slain is a mudabbar or mukatib, qasamah is obligatory and his value is to be paid in three years because the slave is like the free in respect of blood. And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that there is nothing for it because in his view it is in the category of property, and there is no qasamah for a fetus because it is an incomplete creation. Then the author said: 'And if they swear, the blood-money is on the people of the locality, and the guardian does not swear.' Imam al-Shafi'i said: He swears, as mentioned earlier. And our proof is the hadith: 'Fifty men of you swear by Allah: we did not kill him and we do not know his killer, then they pay the blood-money.' The swearer said, 'O Messenger of Allah, swear and pay?' He said: 'Yes.' This is when the claim is against them not as individuals for intentional or mistaken killing, because the defendants are not distinguished from the others. And if he claims against some individuals by name for intentional or mistaken killing, the answer is the same; and the general wording of the book indicates that.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage presents the inter-madhhab dispute on qasamah. The Hanafi position, as stated in the matn, is that when a body is found in a locality and the killer is unknown, fifty men from the locality swear that they did not kill him, and they pay the blood-money. The guardian does not swear. Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik differ. According to al-Shafi'i, if there is lawth (strong suspicion such as a witness or enmity), the guardians of the victim swear fifty oaths and receive blood-money. If no lawth, the defendants are sworn, and if they refuse, the guardians swear and get their claim. Malik goes further: if the claim is intentional killing, qisas (retaliation) is possible. The Hanafi response uses the hadith 'The burden of proof is on the claimant and the oath on the denier' to argue that the oath is on the defendants, not the guardians. The text also discusses cases involving slaves and fetuses, noting that qasamah applies for slaves (except according to a narration from Abu Yusuf) and not for fetuses.

Key Terms
القسامة (al-qasamah): A collective oath taken by fifty men from a locality to deny involvement in an unknown killing, which if sworn, obligates blood-money on the locality.
اللوث (al-lawth): Strong suspicion or evidence indicating the killer, such as a witness (even unjust) or open enmity, used by Shafi'i and Malik to shift the oath to the guardians.
الدية (al-diyah): Blood-money paid as compensation for homicide or injury, fixed amount in Hanafi law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, who swears the oath in a qasamah case?
A) The guardians of the victim
B) The fifty men from the locality where the body was found
C) The ruler
D) The defendant individually

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi qasamah, the oath is always on the defendants (the deniers), and lawth does not shift the oath to the guardian.

Diyat — Blood Money

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Qasamah: Abu Yusuf's Minority View
Discusses Abu Yusuf's alternate ruling on dropping qasamah for some defendants

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the majority Hanafi position from Abu Yusuf's alternate opinion on qasamah and identify which view is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Qasamah liability attaches to the locality as a whole, even if a specific individual is accused—the majority Hanafi view prevails over Abu Yusuf's minority opinion.

This lesson examines a unique intra-Hanafi dispute where Imam Abu Yusuf, in a non-principle narration, diverges from the established majority view on qasamah (collective oath). While the majority holds the entire locality liable for blood-money and oaths, Abu Yusuf argues that if a specific individual is accused, the liability drops from the locality. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to weigh conflicting narrations within the school and apply the principle of istihsan over analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Majority Position
The majority (Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf in principle narrations) holds that qasamah and diyah are due on the entire locality collectively, regardless of whether a specific individual is accused.
2
Recognize Abu Yusuf's Alternate Opinion
In a non-principle narration (nawadir), Abu Yusuf states that if the guardian accuses a specific person from the locality, qasamah drops from the rest; the accused swears one oath, and liability is removed from others. A similar view is reported from Abu Hanifa via Ibn al-Mubarak.
This opinion is not from Zahir al-Riwayah, so it carries less weight.
3
Understand the Qiyas Behind the Alternate View
Analogy would support Abu Yusuf: since the killer might be from outside, the 'āmm (general) texts should not apply. However, the majority invokes istihsan to override analogy because the texts do not differentiate between types of claims.
The illa in qiyas was the possibility of the outsider, but istihsan rejects it.
4
Apply Istihsan and the Generic Texts
The majority argues that the hadiths on qasamah are general ('āmm) and apply to all claims; thus, the locality must swear and pay regardless of the specifics. The general texts (nusūs) are given precedence over analogy.
Istihsan here is based on the implicit preference for the general text.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the majority view: the entire locality is liable. Abu Yusuf's alternate opinion is a minority view recorded in the nawadir, not used for fatwa.
Al-Marghinani and later Hanafi authorities favour the majority via istihsan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعن أبي يوسف في غير رواية الأصول أن القسامة والدية تسقط عن الباقين من أهل المحلة ويقال للولي ألك بينة ؟ فإن قال لا يستحلف المدعى عليه يميناً واحدة وروى ابن المبارك عن أبي حنفية مثله . ووجهه أن القياس يأباه لاحتمال وجود القتل من غيرهم، وفي الاستحسان تجب القسامة والدية على أهل المحلة والنصوص لم تفرق بين دعوى ودعوى فيجاب بإطلاق النصوص لا بالقياس بخلاف ما إذا ادعى على واحد من غيرهم
And from Abu Yusuf in non-principle narration that the qasamah and blood-money drop from the rest of the people of the locality, and the guardian is told: Do you have proof? If he says no, the defendant is sworn one oath. And Ibn al-Mubarak narrated from Abu Hanifa the like. And its justification is that analogy opposes it due to the possibility of the killing from others, but in istihsan, qasamah and blood-money are due on the people of the locality, and the texts did not differentiate between one claim and another, so answer is by the general texts, not by analogy, contrary to if he claimed against one person not from them.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute. The majority Hanafi position (based on the matn and earlier commentary) is that qasamah applies to all people of the locality. However, Imam Abu Yusuf in a non-principle narration (i.e., not from Zahir al-Riwayah) holds that qasamah and liability drop from the rest of the locality if the guardian accuses a specific individual. Instead, the defendant is asked for proof; if none, they swear one oath. This view is also attributed to Abu Hanifa via Ibn al-Mubarak. The text explains that analogy would oppose the majority view because there is no guarantee that the killing didn't come from outside the locality. But istihsan (juristic preference) supports the majority: the texts (hadiths) apply generally regardless of the type of claim. Therefore, the general rule is maintained. The exception is if the accusation is against a single person from outside the locality – then qasamah does not apply to the locality.

Key Terms
الاستحسان (al-istihsān): Juristic preference that overrides analogy; here it justifies imposing liability on the locality despite the possibility of an outside killer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view, what happens when a body is found in a locality and the guardian accuses a specific individual from the locality?
A) The accused swears one oath and no one else is liable
B) The entire locality still bears the qasamah and blood-money
C) The guardian must provide proof or the accused is freed
D) The case is dismissed

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's majority position on qasamah applies the general texts via istihsan, imposing liability on the locality even when a specific individual is accused.

Diyat — Blood Money

The Ruling of Qasamah: Inhabitants Swear, Heir Does Not
Ruling with proof on qasamah for a found corpse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qasamah when a dead body is found, identify the conditions that make it wajib, and explain why the heir does not swear.

Core Idea
Qasamah requires fifty inhabitants to swear, not the heir, based on the Prophet's practice.

When a dead body is found in a locality with strong suspicion (lawth), the inhabitants must collectively swear to deny knowledge of the killing. If they swear, they pay the blood money. The heir does not participate in the oath—a distinctive Hanafi position supported by a hadith of fifty men. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof, and the dispute with Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is qasamah (collective oath). Its hukm is wajib on the inhabitants when there is lawth (strong suspicion). The heir does not swear.
Lawth is a condition; without lawth, different rules apply.
2
Locate the proof
The primary proof is the hadith of fifty men swearing and paying blood money. The author cites it to show that the inhabitants swear and the heir does not.
The hadith is zanni al-thubut but sufficient for wujub.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'يحلف' and the actual practice of the Prophet indicate obligation. The absence of the heir swearing in the hadith proves he does not swear.
This is a direct textual proof overriding qiyas.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Al-Shafi'i holds that the heir swears as well. Abu Yusuf has a transmission limiting qasamah to the accused individual.
The Hanafi tarjih supports Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon position is that the entire locality swears (if lawth exists), and the heir does not swear, based on the general texts and istihsan.
The minority view is rejected as contrary to the explicit hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الديات باب القسامة
ولا علمنا له قاتلاً وإن حلفوا فعلى أهل المحلة الدية ولا يحلف الولي وإن لم يتم العدد هو الذي قتله قتلوه، وإن لم يكن ثم لوث استحلف المدعى عليهم فإن حلفوا لا دية عليهم، وإن أبوا أن يحلفوا حلف المدعي واستحق ما ادعاه لنا قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم «لو أعطى الناس بدعواهم» الحديث . وقوله البينة على المدعي واليمين على من أنكر (١) ولا فرق في ذلك بين الدم والأموال على ظاهر الأحاديث، وما روي في قتيل وجد بين قوم قال يستحلف خمسين رجلاً منهم فهو كقول المؤلف قتيل خرج مخرج الغالب قال في العناية جرح رجل في قبيلة ولم يعلم جارحه فإما أن يصير صاحب فراش أو يكون صحيحاً بحيث يذهب ويجيء، فإن كان الثاني فلا ضمان بالاتفاق، وإن كان الأول ففيه القسامة والدية على القبيلة عند الإمام، وعند الثاني لا شيء فيه اهـ وأطلق في القتيل فشمل الخطأ والعمد والدعوى بذلك قال في الأصل : وإذا وجد قتيل في محلة قوم وادعى ولي القتيل القتل عمداً أو خطأ فهذا على ثلاثة أوجه : إما أن يدعي ولي القتيل على واحد من أهل المحلة أنه هو الذي قتله ،وليه فإن ادعى على جميع أهل المحلة أنهم قتلوا وليه عمداً أو خطأ وادعى على واحد من غير أهل المحلة أنه وليه عمداً أو خطأ وأنكر أهل المحلة فإنه يحلف خمسون رجلاً منهم كل واحد بالله ما قتلته ولا علمت له قاتلاً، فإن حلفوا غرموا الدية وإن نكلوا فإن يحبسهم حتى يحلفهم. وفي الذخيرة : هذا الحبس بدعوى العمد وإن كان يدعي الخطأ فإذا نكلوا عن اليمين يقضى عليهم بالدية اهـ. وقوله يتخيرهم «الولي يعني يختار الصالحين دون الطالحين ولو من أهل الذمة، وإن كان القتيل مدبراً أو مكاتباً وجبت القسامة وقيمته في ثلاثة سنين لأن العبد بمنزلة الأحرار في حق الدماء، وروي عن أبي يوسف أنه لا شيء فيه لأنه في حكم الأموال عنده ولا قسامة في الجنين لأنه ناقص الخلقة اهـ . قال رحمه الله : ( وإن حلفوا فعلى أهل المحلة الدية ولا يحلف الولي) وقال الشافعي رحمه الله : يحلف وقد تقدم ودليلنا قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : يحلف خمسون رجلاً منكم بالله ما قلناه ولا علمنا له قاتلاً ثم أغرموا الدية فقال الحالف : يا رسول الله يحلف ويغرم؟ فقال : نعم الحديث. هذا إذا ادعى عليهم لا بأعيانهم القتل عمداً أو خطأ لأن المدعى عليهم لا يميزون عن الباقين، ولو ادعى على العبض بأعيانهم التقل عمداً أو خطأ فكذلك الجواب وإطلاق الكتاب يدل على ذلك. وعن أبي يوسف في غير رواية الأصول أن القسامة والدية تسقط عن الباقين من أهل المحلة ويقال للولي ألك بينة ؟ فإن قال لا يستحلف المدعى عليه يميناً واحدة وروى ابن المبارك عن أبي حنفية مثله . ووجهه أن القياس Book of Blood Money, Chapter of Qasamah. And if we do not know a killer for him, and they swear, then the inhabitants of the locality are liable for the blood money, and the heir does not swear. And if the number is not complete, he [the heir] is [the one] who killed him, they killed him. And if there is no strong suspicion (lawth), the accused are made to swear; if they swear, there is no blood money on them; and if they refuse to swear, the plaintiff swears and obtains what he claimed. For us is his saying (peace be upon him): 'If people were given according to their claims...' the hadith, and his saying: 'The burden of proof is on the claimant, and the oath is on the denier.' There is no difference in that between blood and property according to the apparent meaning of the hadiths. And what is related about a slain person found among a people, he said: 'Fifty men from among them are made to swear' – it is like the author's statement 'a slain person' issued as a general expression. Al-Inayah said: A man is wounded in a tribe and his injurer is not known: either he becomes bedridden or he is sound such that he goes and comes. If the second, there is no liability by agreement. If the first, then there is qasamah and blood money on the tribe according to the Imam [Abu Hanifa]; according to the second [Abu Yusuf?], there is nothing in it. End. And he spoke generally about the slain person, so it includes error and intent and claim by that. He said in al-Asl: When a slain person is found in a locality of a people, and the heir of the slain claims killing intentionally or by mistake, this is on three aspects: Either the heir claims against one of the inhabitants of the locality that he killed him, or he claims against all the inhabitants that they killed his heir intentionally or by mistake, or he claims against one from outside the inhabitants that he killed him intentionally or by mistake. And the inhabitants deny, then fifty men from them swear each by Allah: 'I did not kill him and I do not know a killer for him.' If they swear, they pay the blood money. If they refuse, he imprisons them until they swear. In al-Dhakhirah: This imprisonment is for a claim of intent; if it is a claim of mistake, then if they refuse the oath, judgment is given against them for the blood money. End. His statement 'the heir chooses them' means he chooses the righteous over the wicked, even if from the people of dhimma. And if the slain is a mudabbar or mukatab, qasamah is obligatory and his value [is due] in three years, because the slave is like a free person regarding blood rights. And it is related from Abu Yusuf that there is nothing in it because in his view it is in the category of property. And there is no qasamah for a fetus because it is of incomplete creation. End. He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'And if they swear, then the inhabitants of the locality are liable for the blood money, and the heir does not swear.' Al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) said: He swears, and it has preceded. And our proof is his saying (peace be upon him): 'Fifty men from among you swear by Allah what we have said and we do not know a killer for him, then they pay the blood money.' The one swearing said: 'O Messenger of Allah, he swears and pays?' He said: 'Yes.' The hadith. This is when he claims against them not as individuals, killing intentionally or by mistake, because the accused are not distinguishable from the rest. And if he claims against some of them as individuals, killing intentionally or by mistake, the answer is similar, and the general application of the book indicates that. And from Abu Yusuf in non-principle transmission that qasamah and blood money drop from the rest of the inhabitants, and it is said to the heir: 'Do you have evidence?' If he says no, the accused swears one oath. And Ibn al-Mubarak related from Abu Hanifa similarly. Its reasoning is that analogy rejects it due to the possibility of killing by others, and in istihsan qasamah and blood money are obligatory on the inhabitants, and the texts did not differentiate between one claim and another, so answer is by the general application of the texts, not by analogy, unlike when he claims against one from outside them.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on qasamah (compurgation) when a dead body is found in a locality. The author first states the basic ruling: if the inhabitants swear that they did not kill nor know the killer, they are liable for the blood money, and the heir does not swear. If there is no strong suspicion (lawth), the accused are made to swear; if they refuse, the plaintiff swears and wins. The proof is the hadith 'If people were given according to their claims...' and the principle that the burden of proof is on the claimant and the oath on the denier. This applies to blood as well as property. The commentary from al-Inayah clarifies the condition of lawth: if the victim was not bedridden, there is no liability; if bedridden, qasamah and blood money are on the tribe according to Abu Hanifa, but Abu Yusuf disagrees. The text then cites al-Asl, detailing three scenarios of claim: against one inhabitant, against all, or against an outsider. In each case, fifty men from the locality swear. If they refuse, they are imprisoned until they swear (for intentional killing) or judgment is given (for mistake). The heir may choose righteous candidates, including dhimmis. For slaves (mudabbar, mukatab), qasamah is due and value is paid over three years, but Abu Yusuf exempts them as property. No qasamah for a fetus due to incomplete creation. The passage then addresses al-Shafi'i's view that the heir swears; the Hanafi proof is the hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) had fifty men swear and then pay blood money, showing that the heir does not swear. The ruling applies whether the claim is against all or against specific individuals. An intra-Hanafi transmission from Abu Yusuf holds that only the accused individual swears one oath, but the relied-upon position (istihsan) is that the entire locality swears, as per the general texts.

Key Terms
قسامة (qasamah): A type of collective oath taken by the inhabitants of a locality when a dead body is found, to exculpate themselves from liability for blood money.
لوث (lawth): A strong presumption that the killing was done by the inhabitants, such as the victim being found in their locality with signs of violence.
ولي (wali): The legal heir of the victim who has the right to claim blood money or qisas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The heir of the victim
B) Fifty men from the inhabitants
C) Both the heir and the inhabitants
D) Only the accused individual

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that in qasamah, the inhabitants of the locality swear fifty oaths to deny liability, and the heir does not swear, based on the explicit hadith of the Prophet.
